### Advanced Skills
**Query:** "List all advanced calisthenics skills with: skill name, prerequisites, progression steps, muscles worked. Include: planche, handstand push-up, back lever, human flag progressions."

**Response:**
```
COMPLETED BY CLAUDE (DETAILED VERSION)

## ADVANCED CALISTHENICS OVERVIEW

Advanced calisthenics represents the **pinnacle of bodyweight training**—skills that most people will never achieve, requiring years of dedicated practice. These movements demand extraordinary strength-to-weight ratios, extensive conditioning of connective tissue, and refined neurological control.

**Reality Check - Timeline Expectations:**
- **Planche**: 2-6+ years for full (most never achieve)
- **Full Front Lever**: 1-3 years
- **Back Lever**: 6 months - 2 years
- **Human Flag**: 1-3 years
- **One-Arm Pull-Up**: 1-3 years
- **Freestanding HSPU**: 1-2 years

These timelines assume:
- Already intermediate level (can do 15+ pull-ups, muscle-ups, etc.)
- Consistent training (4-6 days/week with dedicated skill work)
- Proper nutrition and recovery
- Injury-free progression

**Why Some People Progress Faster:**
- **Lower body weight** (lighter = easier due to physics)
- **Favorable limb proportions** (shorter limbs = shorter levers = easier)
- **Training history** (gymnasts have massive head start)
- **Age** (younger bodies adapt faster)
- **Genetics** (muscle fiber composition, tendon strength)

**The Importance of Connective Tissue:**
Advanced skills require not just muscle strength but **conditioned tendons, ligaments, and joints**. Connective tissue adapts 3-10x slower than muscle. This is why progression must be gradual—your muscles might be ready for the next step, but your tendons might not be. **Tendon injuries (especially biceps tendon in lever work) end careers.**

---

## PLANCHE PROGRESSIONS

**The planche is arguably the most difficult calisthenics skill**, requiring you to hold your body horizontal face-down while supported only on your hands with elbows locked. It defies intuitive physics—your entire body weight is balanced over a base the size of your hands.

**Muscles Worked:** Anterior deltoids (primary—extreme demand), pectoralis major, triceps, biceps (isometric stabilization), serratus anterior (scapular protraction), core (entire), wrist flexors

**Prerequisites (Solid Foundation Required):**
- 30+ diamond push-ups
- 60 second planche lean
- Strong, flexible wrists
- 30 second frog stand
- Generally: 2+ years of calisthenics training

**Biomechanics - Why Planche Is So Hard:**
The planche violates normal physics. Your hands are near your hips, but your body extends forward. To balance, your shoulders must produce enormous forward lean force. The further your legs extend, the longer the lever, the more shoulder strength required. Each body segment adds exponentially more difficulty.

**Statistics:**
- ~2% of dedicated calisthenics practitioners ever achieve a full planche
- ~10-15% achieve a straddle planche
- ~30-40% can hold an advanced tuck planche for 10+ seconds

| Step | Exercise | Target to Progress | Detailed Technique |
|------|----------|-------------------|-------------------|
| 1 | **Planche Lean** | 30-60 seconds | Push-up position but lean shoulders far forward of hands (shoulders over fingertips, not over wrists). Keep arms locked. **Builds forward lean strength** needed for planche. Lean as far forward as possible while maintaining position. |
| 2 | **Frog Stand (Crow Pose)** | 30 seconds | Hands on floor, knees resting on back of upper arms, lean forward until feet lift off. **Teaches balance point** and builds wrist strength/flexibility. Not a true planche position (bent arms) but foundational. |
| 3 | **Tucked Planche** | 15-20 seconds | Hands on floor/parallettes, lean forward, lift feet with knees tucked tight to chest, arms LOCKED. **First true planche variation.** Hips should be level with shoulders. Protract scapulae hard (push shoulders forward). |
| 4 | **Advanced Tuck Planche** | 10-15 seconds | Same as tucked but back is flat/horizontal (not rounded). Hips at same height as shoulders. **Significantly harder than tucked.** Requires more strength to maintain flat back position. |
| 5 | **One-Leg Planche** | 10 seconds each | Advanced tuck but one leg extended, one tucked. **Asymmetric progression** toward straddle. Alternate legs. |
| 6 | **Straddle Planche** | 5-10 seconds | Legs fully extended but spread wide (straddled). **First extended-leg variation.** Reduced lever compared to full. Still extremely impressive achievement—most stop here. |
| 7 | **Half-Lay Planche** | 5 seconds | Legs together but hips piked slightly (body forms slight "7"). **Transition to full.** |
| 8 | **Full Planche** | 3+ seconds | Body perfectly horizontal, legs together, arms locked. **The ultimate achievement.** Very few ever reach this level. |

**Planche Training Tips:**
- **Parallettes** reduce wrist strain and allow better wrist angle—highly recommended
- **Pseudo planche push-ups** (PPPUs): Push-ups in planche lean position, touching hands to hips
- **Band-assisted planche**: Band around hips attached overhead to reduce load while learning position
- **Frequency**: Can practice planche holds 4-6x per week (it's neurological, not just strength)
- **Protect your wrists**: Proper warm-up and flexibility work is mandatory

**Common Planche Mistakes:**
- **Bent elbows**: Arms must be locked—bent elbows is a different skill
- **Not leaning forward enough**: Shoulders must be well in front of hands
- **Scapulae not protracted**: Must push shoulders forward (protract)
- **Hips too high**: Body should be horizontal, not piked up

---

## HANDSTAND PUSH-UP PROGRESSIONS

**The handstand push-up (HSPU)** is an overhead press while inverted—moving your entire body weight through vertical pressing. It builds tremendous shoulder and triceps strength.

**Muscles Worked:** Anterior deltoids, lateral deltoids, triceps, upper chest, trapezius, core (balance), wrist stabilizers

**Prerequisites:**
- 60 second wall handstand hold (or 30 sec freestanding)
- 20+ parallel bar dips
- 15+ pike push-ups
- Basic handstand balance competency

**Wall vs. Freestanding:**
- **Wall HSPU**: Back or chest to wall, provides balance assistance. Most people train here.
- **Freestanding HSPU**: No wall, requires balance AND strength simultaneously. Significantly harder.

| Step | Exercise | Target to Progress | Detailed Technique |
|------|----------|-------------------|-------------------|
| 1 | **Pike Push-Ups** | 15-20 reps | Downward dog position, perform push-ups bringing head toward floor. **Builds overhead pressing pattern.** Higher hips = harder. |
| 2 | **Elevated Pike Push-Ups** | 12-15 reps | Feet elevated on box/bench in pike position. Higher elevation = more vertical = harder. **Progressive loading toward vertical.** |
| 3 | **Wall Handstand Hold** | 60 seconds | Handstand facing wall (belly to wall preferred for better alignment) or back to wall. **Builds positional strength** and acclimates body to inverted pressing. |
| 4 | **Wall Handstand Negatives** | 5-8 reps × 5 sec | From handstand, lower slowly for 5 seconds until head touches, kick back up or lower down. **Eccentric HSPU strength.** Control the descent. |
| 5 | **Partial Wall HSPU** | 8-10 reps | Lower to half or 3/4 depth, push back up. **Builds concentric strength through partial ROM.** Gradually increase depth. |
| 6 | **Full Wall HSPU** | 5-8 reps | Full ROM—lower until head touches floor, press back to lockout. **Full handstand push-up.** Keep core tight, don't arch excessively. |
| 7 | **Deficit Wall HSPU** | 5-8 reps | Hands on parallettes or blocks, lower head BELOW hand level. **Increased ROM** builds strength through fuller range. |
| 8 | **Freestanding HSPU** | 1+ rep | Full HSPU with no wall assistance. **The ultimate achievement.** Requires balance mastery plus strength. Few achieve this. |

**HSPU Technique Keys:**
- **Stack the joints**: Wrists, elbows, shoulders in line
- **Elbow direction**: Slight forward, not flared to sides
- **Core tight**: Don't over-arch—maintain hollow-ish body
- **Head path**: Head moves slightly forward of hands at bottom (tripod position)
- **Press straight up**: Not forward or backward

**Training the Handstand Separately:**
HSPU requires handstand competency. If you can't hold a handstand, work on that first:
- Wall holds (belly to wall)
- Kick-up practice
- Balance drills (toe pulls, heel pulls)
- Freestanding attempts daily

---

## BACK LEVER PROGRESSIONS

**The back lever** is a horizontal hold face-down from a bar with arms behind you. While visually similar to front lever (but inverted), it's generally **easier** due to favorable leverage and uses different muscles (biceps vs. lats).

**Muscles Worked:** Biceps (extreme—supinated/straight-arm position), posterior deltoids, pectoralis major, latissimus dorsi, core (maintaining body line)

**Prerequisites:**
- 10+ pull-ups
- Good shoulder flexibility (German hang comfortable)
- Basic front lever work (helps with body tension)
- Skin the cat ability

**Bicep Warning:**
Back lever places **extreme stress on the biceps tendon** at the elbow. The straight-arm supinated position under load is dangerous if you're not conditioned. **Progress slowly and listen to pain signals.** Bicep tendon injuries are common in rush progressions.

| Step | Exercise | Target to Progress | Detailed Technique |
|------|----------|-------------------|-------------------|
| 1 | **German Hang (Skin the Cat)** | 30 seconds comfortable | From hanging, pull through to inverted hang, continue rotating until arms are behind you in back lever position (but inverted/vertical). **Builds shoulder flexibility** and conditions biceps for back lever position. Must be comfortable here first. |
| 2 | **Tucked Back Lever** | 15-20 seconds | From inverted hang, lower body to horizontal with knees tucked tight to chest. **First back lever variation.** Arms straight, body horizontal face-down. Retract scapulae. |
| 3 | **Advanced Tuck Back Lever** | 10-15 seconds | Same but with back flat/horizontal (not rounded). Hips level with shoulders. **Increased difficulty.** |
| 4 | **Single-Leg Back Lever** | 10 seconds each | One leg extended, one tucked. **Asymmetric progression.** |
| 5 | **Straddle Back Lever** | 5-10 seconds | Legs extended and spread wide. **First full-extension variation.** |
| 6 | **Full Back Lever** | 5+ seconds | Body horizontal, legs together and extended. **Complete skill.** Easier than front lever for most people due to biomechanics. |

**Back Lever vs. Front Lever:**
Back lever is typically **easier** because:
- Biceps are stronger in the back lever position than lats are in front lever position
- Favorable leverage angles
- Less core demand

**Safety Note:**
If you feel **any elbow pain or bicep discomfort**, stop immediately. Condition gradually—spend extra time in German hang before attempting lever holds.

---

## HUMAN FLAG PROGRESSIONS

**The human flag** is a side-horizontal hold on a vertical pole—your body perpendicular to the pole, held up by your arms. It's an incredible display of lateral core strength and shoulder stability.

**Muscles Worked:** Obliques (extreme demand—anti-lateral flexion), latissimus dorsi (top arm pulling), deltoids (bottom arm pushing), entire core, shoulders

**Prerequisites:**
- 45+ second side plank each side
- 10+ pull-ups
- 20+ push-ups
- Strong press (dips/HSPU work)
- Understanding that bottom arm PUSHES, top arm PULLS

**The Physics:**
Human flag is a **push-pull** exercise. Your bottom arm pushes UP on the pole (like a one-arm side push-up), your top arm pulls DOWN (like a one-arm side pull-up). Your obliques prevent your body from bending/falling.

| Step | Exercise | Target to Progress | Detailed Technique |
|------|----------|-------------------|-------------------|
| 1 | **Side Plank** | 45-60 seconds each | Standard side plank. **Builds lateral core foundation.** Must be solid here. |
| 2 | **Vertical Flag Hold** | 15 seconds | On vertical pole/stall bars, grip with both hands, position body vertical (feet toward ceiling). **Teaches hand position and basic press/pull.** Easier than horizontal. |
| 3 | **Tucked Human Flag** | 10-15 seconds | Same as above but lower body toward horizontal with knees tucked. **First horizontal variation.** Intense oblique demand begins. |
| 4 | **Advanced Tuck Human Flag** | 8-10 seconds | Knees less tucked, body more horizontal. **Increased lever length.** |
| 5 | **Straddle Human Flag** | 5-8 seconds | Legs extended but spread wide. **First full-extension variation.** Very impressive achievement. |
| 6 | **One-Leg Human Flag** | 5-8 seconds | One leg extended, one tucked. **Transition to full.** |
| 7 | **Full Human Flag** | 3-5 seconds | Body perfectly horizontal, legs together. **Ultimate lateral strength display.** |

**Human Flag Tips:**
- **Equipment matters**: Need sturdy vertical pole or wall bars (stall bars). Diameter affects grip.
- **Hand position**: Bottom hand palm away, fingers down. Top hand palm toward you, fingers up.
- **Push AND pull**: Both arms work simultaneously—don't neglect the bottom arm push.
- **Supplementary exercises**: One-arm push-up progressions, heavy side planks, pull-up variations

---

## ONE-ARM PULL-UP PROGRESSIONS

**The one-arm pull-up (OAP)** is exactly what it sounds like—a pull-up using one arm only. It requires incredible relative strength and years of dedicated training.

**Muscles Worked:** Latissimus dorsi (unilateral—massive demand), biceps brachii, brachialis, core (anti-rotation), forearm flexors (grip)

**Prerequisites (Non-Negotiable):**
- 20+ strict pull-ups
- Weighted pull-up with +50% bodyweight × 5 reps
- Ability to do archer pull-ups
- Strong grip

**Why 20 Pull-Ups Isn't Enough:**
A one-arm pull-up requires approximately **double** the pulling force per arm as a two-arm pull-up. But due to anti-rotation demands and changed leverage, you need **more than twice** the strength. Most estimates say you need to pull 175-200% of bodyweight to do a OAP.

| Step | Exercise | Target to Progress | Detailed Technique |
|------|----------|-------------------|-------------------|
| 1 | **Weighted Pull-Ups** | +50% BW × 5 reps | Add weight via belt/vest until pulling at least 1.5x bodyweight total for 5 reps. **Builds raw pulling strength needed for OAP.** |
| 2 | **Archer Pull-Ups** | 5-8 each side | Wide grip, pull toward one hand while other arm extends straight to side (assisting minimally). **Unilateral loading progression.** Keep assisting arm as straight as possible. |
| 3 | **One-Arm Assisted (Towel/Band)** | 3-5 each | Grip bar with one hand, other hand holds towel draped over bar (or band). Pull up using minimal assistance from towel hand. **Trains the movement pattern** with reduced load. |
| 4 | **One-Arm Negatives** | 3-5 each × 5 sec | Jump to top, remove one hand, lower slowly for 5 seconds on one arm. **Eccentric OAP strength.** Must control the descent fully. |
| 5 | **One-Arm Pull-Up** | 1+ each arm | Dead hang on one arm, pull chin above bar. **Achievement of a lifetime.** Very few ever reach this level. |

**OAP Training Considerations:**
- **Elbow health**: One-arm pulling stresses the elbow significantly. Build up gradually.
- **Grip work**: Your grip must be strong enough to hold bodyweight one-handed during the pull.
- **Anti-rotation**: Your core fights rotation throughout—strong obliques help.
- **Supinated vs. Pronated**: Supinated (chin-up grip) is typically easier for OAP.

---

## CALISTHENICS MASTERY HIERARCHY

**Level 1 - Foundation:**
- Push-ups (20+)
- Pull-ups (10+)
- Dips (10+)
- Squats (20+)

**Level 2 - Competent:**
- L-Sit (15 seconds)
- Pistol Squat
- Muscle-Up (kipping)
- 20+ Pull-ups

**Level 3 - Intermediate:**
- Strict Muscle-Up
- Dragon Flag
- Wall HSPU
- 30 second L-Sit

**Level 4 - Advanced:**
- Front Lever (5+ seconds)
- Back Lever
- Freestanding HSPU
- Straddle Planche

**Level 5 - Elite:**
- Full Planche
- One-Arm Pull-Up
- Full Human Flag
- Iron Cross
- Maltese
- Victorian

**Final Notes on Advanced Skills:**

1. **Not everyone will achieve these**: Genetics, body type, and time investment all matter. Partial achievements (straddle variations) are still impressive.

2. **Injury prevention is paramount**: These skills stress connective tissue tremendously. Progress slowly. Take deload weeks. Address pain immediately.

3. **Specificity matters**: If you want the planche, train planche progressions specifically. General strength helps but doesn't transfer fully.

4. **Consistency over intensity**: Daily practice of 15-30 minutes beats occasional 2-hour sessions.

5. **Document your journey**: These skills take years. Track progress, celebrate milestones.

**Sources:**
- Overcoming Gravity 2nd Edition (Steven Low) - The bible of calisthenics programming
- Building the Gymnastic Body (Christopher Sommer)
- FitnessFAQs - Advanced skill tutorials
- Calisthenics Unity - Community standards
- GMB Fitness - Movement quality focus
- Scientific literature on straight-arm strength and lever mechanics
```

---

## 1.8 Warmup Exercises

### Upper Body Warmups
**Query:** "List all upper body warmup exercises for before chest/back/shoulder/arm workouts with: name, duration/reps, muscles targeted, when to use (which workout days)."

**Response:**
```
COMPLETED BY CLAUDE (DETAILED VERSION)

## THE SCIENCE OF WARMING UP

A proper warmup is **not optional**—it's a critical component of training that directly impacts performance, injury risk, and long-term progress. Understanding why we warm up informs how to warm up effectively.

**Physiological Benefits of Warming Up:**
1. **Increased muscle temperature**: Warmer muscles contract more forcefully and relax faster. A 1°C increase in muscle temp improves performance by ~2-5%.
2. **Enhanced blood flow**: Redirects blood from organs to working muscles, delivering oxygen and nutrients.
3. **Reduced muscle viscosity**: Warmer muscles have less internal resistance, allowing smoother, more efficient contractions.
4. **Improved nerve conduction**: Nervous system signals travel faster at higher temperatures.
5. **Increased synovial fluid production**: Joint "lubrication" reduces friction and protects cartilage.
6. **Prepared connective tissue**: Tendons and ligaments become more pliable, reducing strain injury risk.
7. **Mental readiness**: Shifts focus from daily stress to training.

**Dynamic vs. Static Stretching (Pre-Workout):**
Research is clear: **dynamic stretching is superior before exercise** while static stretching can actually REDUCE performance.

- **Static stretching pre-workout** can reduce power output by 5-30% and weaken muscles for up to an hour (Behm & Chaouachi, 2011)
- **Dynamic stretching** increases performance, especially in activities requiring power and speed
- Save static stretching for POST-workout or dedicated mobility sessions

**Warmup Structure (The RAMP Protocol):**
1. **R - Raise**: Elevate heart rate, body temperature, breathing (light cardio)
2. **A - Activate**: Wake up key muscles that may be dormant (glute activation, rotator cuff work)
3. **M - Mobilize**: Move joints through full range of motion (dynamic stretches)
4. **P - Potentiate**: Practice movement patterns with increasing intensity (warmup sets)

---

## SHOULDER WARMUP (MANDATORY BEFORE ALL UPPER BODY WORK)

The shoulder is the **most mobile and least stable joint** in the body, making it extremely injury-prone. Shoulder warmup is non-negotiable.

| Exercise | Duration/Reps | Primary Target | Detailed Technique |
|----------|---------------|----------------|-------------------|
| **Arm Circles (Progressive)** | 15 forward, 15 backward (small→large) | Deltoids, rotator cuff | Start with small circles, progressively increase size. Keep core engaged. Don't just swing—control the movement. **Elevates shoulder temperature and synovial fluid production.** |
| **Band Pull-Aparts** | 15-25 reps | Rear deltoids, rhomboids, rotator cuff | Hold light band in front, arms straight at shoulder height, pull apart until band touches chest. **Activates posterior shoulder muscles** that are often weak/inactive. Critical for shoulder health. Use light band—this is activation, not strength. |
| **Band Dislocates (Pass-Throughs)** | 10-15 reps | Rotator cuff, anterior deltoids, chest | Hold band (or PVC pipe) wide, arms straight, slowly rotate overhead and behind back, return. **Improves shoulder flexibility** through full ROM. Go slow—no bouncing. Wider grip = easier. Narrow grip as you progress. |
| **Wall Slides (Wall Angels)** | 10-15 reps | Scapular stabilizers (serratus, lower traps) | Back against wall, arms in "W" position, slide up to "Y" while keeping contact with wall. **Activates often-dormant scapular muscles** and trains upward rotation. If hard to maintain contact, you have mobility issues to address. |
| **YTWL Raises** | 8-10 each position | Rotator cuff, lower traps, rhomboids | Bent over or lying face-down, make Y-T-W-L shapes with arms using light weight or no weight. **Comprehensive rotator cuff activation.** Each position hits different muscles. |
| **Shoulder Rolls** | 15 forward, 15 backward | Trapezius, levator scapulae | Roll shoulders in circles. Simple but effective for **releasing upper trap tension** accumulated from sitting/stress. |
| **Cat-Cow** | 10 reps | Thoracic spine, erector spinae | On all fours, alternate between arching back (cow) and rounding back (cat). **Mobilizes thoracic spine** which is crucial for overhead movements and bench press. |
| **Thread the Needle** | 8 each side | Thoracic spine, shoulders | On all fours, thread one arm under torso rotating thoracic spine, return and reach to ceiling. **Thoracic rotation** improves pressing mechanics. |
| **Face Pulls (Light Band)** | 15-20 reps | Rear delts, external rotators | Pull band to face, externally rotating shoulders, squeeze shoulder blades. **Balances internal rotation dominance** from pressing. |

---

## CHEST DAY SPECIFIC WARMUP

Chest day primarily involves pressing movements that stress the shoulder joint and pectorals. Warmup must prepare both.

| Exercise | Duration/Reps | Primary Target | When/Why |
|----------|---------------|----------------|----------|
| **Doorway Chest Stretch (Dynamic)** | 20 pulses each arm | Pectoralis major/minor | Arm on doorframe at 90°, lean through gently with small pulses (not static hold). **Opens tight pecs** that may be shortened from sitting. Dynamic version only pre-workout. |
| **Scapular Push-Ups** | 10-15 reps | Serratus anterior, scapular control | Push-up position, arms locked, only move by protracting (pushing apart) and retracting (squeezing together) shoulder blades. **Activates serratus** for proper pressing mechanics. |
| **Light Band Press** | 15-20 reps | Pectorals, triceps, anterior delts | Press light band away from chest horizontally. **Blood flow and movement rehearsal** without loading the joints. Focus on squeeze at end. |
| **Walk-Outs (Inchworms)** | 5-8 reps | Full body, emphasis on pressing muscles | From standing, fold over, walk hands out to plank, walk back, stand. **Full body primer** that stretches hamstrings and loads pressing muscles. |
| **Push-Up (Slow Tempo)** | 8-10 reps | Chest, shoulders, triceps | Full push-ups with 3-sec descent, 1-sec ascent. **Rehearses pressing pattern** before adding load. |

**Warmup Sets for Bench Press:**
After the above, progress with barbell warmup sets:
- Empty bar × 10-15 reps
- 40% working weight × 8 reps
- 60% working weight × 5 reps
- 80% working weight × 3 reps
- Begin working sets

---

## BACK DAY SPECIFIC WARMUP

Back training involves pulling movements that heavily load the lats, rhomboids, and biceps. The spine also needs attention for deadlift days.

| Exercise | Duration/Reps | Primary Target | When/Why |
|----------|---------------|----------------|----------|
| **Lat Stretch (Overhead)** | 20-30 sec each side | Latissimus dorsi | Hang from bar or hold doorframe overhead, lean away to stretch lat. **Opens tight lats** for full ROM in pulling. Dynamic version = gentle pulses. |
| **Dead Hang** | 20-30 sec | Lats, grip, shoulders, spine | Hang from bar with straight arms, relax into the hang. **Decompresses spine, stretches lats, builds grip.** Allow shoulders to elevate fully (passive hang). |
| **Scapular Pulls (Active Hang)** | 10-15 reps | Scapular depressors/retractors | From dead hang, pull shoulder blades down and back (depressing), raising body 1-2 inches without bending elbows. **Activates the muscles that initiate pulling movements.** |
| **Band Rows** | 15-20 reps | Lats, rhomboids, rear delts | Light band row focusing on squeezing shoulder blades together at peak. **Movement rehearsal and muscle activation.** |
| **Arm Huggers** | 10 each direction | Upper back, shoulders | Cross arms in front and wrap around yourself, alternate which arm is on top. **Dynamic stretch for upper back.** |
| **Hip Hinge Practice** | 10 reps | Hamstrings, glutes, erector spinae (for deadlift days) | Bodyweight hip hinge (RDL motion) to groove the pattern. **Prepares for loaded hip hinge movements.** |
| **Cat-Cow** | 10 reps | Spinal erectors, thoracic mobility | Arch and round the spine. **Mobilizes spine before loaded pulling.** |

---

## ARM DAY SPECIFIC WARMUP

Arm work (biceps, triceps) heavily stresses the elbow joint and wrists. These structures need specific preparation.

| Exercise | Duration/Reps | Primary Target | When/Why |
|----------|---------------|----------------|----------|
| **Wrist Circles** | 15 each direction, each wrist | Wrist flexors/extensors | Circle wrists slowly in both directions. **Lubricates wrist joint** essential for curls and pressing. |
| **Wrist Flexion/Extension** | 10 each direction | Forearm muscles | Extend hand palm down, gently pull fingers back; then pull fingers forward. **Dynamic wrist stretch.** |
| **Elbow Circles** | 10 each direction | Elbow joint | With hands on shoulders, make circles with elbows. **Increases synovial fluid in elbow joint.** |
| **Light Band Curls** | 15-20 reps | Biceps | Light resistance curls focusing on muscle contraction. **Blood flow to biceps** without fatigue. |
| **Light Band Pushdowns** | 15-20 reps | Triceps | Light band overhead tricep extension or pushdown. **Activates triceps** for pressing work. |
| **Finger Extensions (with Band)** | 15-20 reps | Forearm extensors | Band around fingers, spread fingers apart against resistance. **Balances grip work** and prevents elbow issues. |
| **Prayer Stretch** | 15 sec | Wrist flexors | Palms together, fingers up, lower hands while keeping palms together. **Wrist flexor stretch.** |

---

## COMPLETE UPPER BODY WARMUP STRUCTURE (8-12 minutes)

1. **Raise (2-3 min)**: Jumping jacks, arm swings, rowing machine, or jump rope until light sweat
2. **Activate (2-3 min)**: Band pull-aparts, YTWL raises, face pulls
3. **Mobilize (2-3 min)**: Arm circles, band dislocates, cat-cow, thread the needle
4. **Potentiate (2-3 min)**: Movement-specific warmup sets, ramping to working weight

**Remember**: A good warmup takes 8-12 minutes. This is NOT wasted time—it's an investment in performance and longevity.
```

---

### Lower Body Warmups
**Query:** "List all lower body warmup exercises for before leg workouts with: name, duration/reps, muscles targeted, purpose."

**Response:**
```
COMPLETED BY CLAUDE (DETAILED VERSION)

## LOWER BODY WARMUP FUNDAMENTALS

Lower body training involves the largest muscle groups and often the heaviest loads. The warmup must address:
- **Hip mobility** (the hip is a deep ball-and-socket joint that stiffens from sitting)
- **Glute activation** (the glutes are often "asleep" from prolonged sitting—glute amnesia)
- **Knee and ankle preparation** (load-bearing joints need synovial fluid production)
- **Nervous system priming** (heavy lifts like squats/deadlifts require CNS readiness)

**Why Glute Activation Matters:**
Modern lifestyles (sitting 8+ hours daily) cause "glute amnesia"—the gluteal muscles become inhibited and stop firing properly. This leads to:
- Overuse of hamstrings and lower back during hip extension
- Knee valgus (caving in) during squats
- Reduced power output
- Increased injury risk

Activation exercises "wake up" the neural connection to the glutes before loading them.

---

## HIP MOBILITY EXERCISES

| Exercise | Duration/Reps | Primary Target | Detailed Technique |
|----------|---------------|----------------|-------------------|
| **Hip Circles** | 10 each direction, each leg | Hip joint (all directions) | Stand on one leg, circle other leg in large circles forward and backward. **Moves hip through full ROM** and promotes synovial fluid production. Don't rush—controlled circles. |
| **Leg Swings (Front-Back)** | 15 each leg | Hip flexors, hamstrings | Hold support, swing leg forward and backward with increasing amplitude. **Dynamic hip flexor/hamstring stretch.** Let momentum increase naturally—don't force ROM. |
| **Leg Swings (Side-to-Side)** | 15 each leg | Adductors, abductors | Same as above but swing leg across body and out to side. **Opens inner and outer hip.** Important for squat depth. |
| **90/90 Hip Switches** | 10 reps total | Hip internal/external rotators | Sit with one leg in front (external rotation) and one to side (internal rotation), switch positions fluidly. **Improves hip rotation mobility** needed for deep squats. |
| **World's Greatest Stretch** | 5-8 each side | Hip flexors, hamstrings, thoracic spine, groin | Lunge position, place same-side elbow to floor inside front foot, rotate and reach opposite arm to ceiling. **The single best dynamic stretch** that addresses multiple areas. Do this every leg day. |
| **Deep Squat Hold** | 30-60 seconds | Hips, ankles, groin, lower back | Squat to full depth, hold position. Use counterweight or hold onto something if needed. **Prepares joints for squatting position.** Shift weight side to side, rotate slightly. |
| **Kneeling Hip Flexor Stretch (Dynamic)** | 10 pulses each side | Hip flexors (iliopsoas, rectus femoris) | Kneeling lunge position, squeeze glute of back leg, pulse forward gently. **Dynamically opens hip flexors** that tighten from sitting. Don't static hold pre-workout. |
| **Pigeon Pose (Dynamic)** | 10 pulses each side | Hip external rotators, glutes | Front leg bent in front, back leg extended behind, pulse down gently. **Opens hip external rotators.** Dynamic version only pre-workout. |
| **Frog Stretch (Dynamic)** | 10 pulses | Adductors, groin | On all fours, spread knees wide, rock back and forth. **Opens adductors** for wide-stance squats and sumo deadlifts. |

---

## GLUTE ACTIVATION EXERCISES

| Exercise | Duration/Reps | Primary Target | Detailed Technique |
|----------|---------------|----------------|-------------------|
| **Glute Bridge** | 15-20 reps | Gluteus maximus | Lie on back, feet flat, drive through heels to lift hips until body straight from knees to shoulders, squeeze glutes hard at top. **Foundation glute activation.** Don't hyperextend lower back—keep core engaged. |
| **Single-Leg Glute Bridge** | 10 each side | Gluteus maximus (unilateral) | Same as above but one leg extended. **Addresses side-to-side imbalances** and increases intensity. |
| **Clamshells** | 15 each side | Gluteus medius | Lie on side, knees bent 90°, feet together, open top knee like a clamshell. **Activates gluteus medius** which stabilizes the pelvis during squats. Band optional for added resistance. |
| **Banded Lateral Walks (Monster Walks)** | 15 steps each direction | Gluteus medius/minimus | Band around thighs above knees, athletic stance, step sideways maintaining tension. **Excellent pre-squat medius activation.** Don't let knees cave in. |
| **Fire Hydrants** | 12 each side | Gluteus medius, hip external rotators | On all fours, lift knee out to side (like a dog at a fire hydrant). **Hip abduction activation** in different position than clamshells. |
| **Donkey Kicks** | 12 each side | Gluteus maximus | On all fours, kick one leg back and up, squeezing glute at top. **Hip extension activation.** Don't hyperextend lower back—movement is from hip. |
| **Bird Dog** | 10 each side | Glutes, core, back extensors | On all fours, extend opposite arm and leg simultaneously. **Glute activation with core stability demand.** Keep hips level—don't rotate. |

**Glute Activation Test:**
Before squatting, do a single-leg glute bridge. Do you feel it primarily in your GLUTE or your HAMSTRING? If hamstring, your glutes aren't firing properly—do more activation work.

---

## KNEE & ANKLE PREPARATION

| Exercise | Duration/Reps | Primary Target | Detailed Technique |
|----------|---------------|----------------|-------------------|
| **Bodyweight Squats** | 15-20 reps | Full lower body | Full depth squats with no weight. **Grooves the pattern** and increases synovial fluid in knees and hips. Focus on perfect form. |
| **Walking Lunges** | 10 each leg | Quads, glutes, hip flexors | Step forward into lunge, knee to near-floor, push through to next step. **Dynamic leg preparation** that opens hip flexors of back leg. |
| **Ankle Circles** | 15 each direction, each ankle | Ankle joint | Circle ankle slowly in both directions. **Ankle mobility is critical for squat depth.** Stiff ankles cause forward lean, heels rising, or knee cave. |
| **Ankle Dorsiflexion Mobilization** | 10 reps each side | Tibialis anterior, ankle joint | In lunge position, drive front knee over toes as far as possible while keeping heel down. **Increases dorsiflexion** needed for deep squats. |
| **Calf Raises** | 15-20 reps | Gastrocnemius, soleus | Stand on both feet or single leg, raise onto balls of feet, lower slowly. **Blood flow to calves** and ankle stability. |
| **High Knees** | 20-30 sec | Hip flexors, quads | Run in place driving knees high. **Cardio + hip flexor activation.** Elevates heart rate. |
| **Butt Kicks** | 20-30 sec | Hamstrings | Run in place kicking heels toward glutes. **Hamstring activation** and cardio. |

---

## COMPLETE LOWER BODY WARMUP SEQUENCE (10-12 minutes)

**Phase 1: Raise Heart Rate (2 min)**
- Light cycling, walking, or jogging
- OR: 30 sec jumping jacks → 30 sec high knees → 30 sec butt kicks → 30 sec jogging

**Phase 2: Hip Mobility (3 min)**
- Hip circles: 10 each direction each leg
- Leg swings (front-back): 10 each leg
- Leg swings (side-to-side): 10 each leg
- World's Greatest Stretch: 5 each side
- Deep squat hold: 30 sec

**Phase 3: Glute Activation (3 min)**
- Glute bridges: 15 reps
- Clamshells: 12 each side
- Banded lateral walks: 10 steps each direction
- Fire hydrants: 10 each side

**Phase 4: Movement Preparation (2 min)**
- Bodyweight squats: 15 reps
- Walking lunges: 8 each leg
- Single-leg glute bridges: 8 each side (test glute firing)

**Phase 5: Warmup Sets (varies)**
For squats:
- Empty bar × 10
- 40% × 8
- 60% × 5
- 80% × 3
- Begin working sets

**Signs Your Warmup Is Complete:**
- Light sweat
- Elevated breathing (but not fatigued)
- Hips feel "open"
- Glutes feel activated (you can feel them firing)
- Joints feel lubricated (no stiffness)
```

---

### Full Body Dynamic Warmups
**Query:** "List all dynamic warmup exercises for general full body activation with: name, duration/reps, muscles targeted, purpose."

**Response:**
```
COMPLETED BY CLAUDE (DETAILED VERSION)

## FULL BODY DYNAMIC WARMUP OVERVIEW

A full-body dynamic warmup is used before:
- Full-body training sessions
- Sports/athletic activities
- Any activity where specific warmup isn't feasible
- General exercise classes

The goal is to **raise body temperature, increase range of motion, activate key muscles, and prepare the nervous system**—all in 5-10 minutes.

**Dynamic Warmup Principles:**
1. **Start slow, increase intensity**: Begin with gentle movements, progressively increase amplitude and speed
2. **Move in all planes**: Forward/back, side-to-side, rotational—the body moves in 3D
3. **Work from ground up (or head down)**: Systematic approach ensures nothing is missed
4. **Mimic upcoming activities**: If you're about to sprint, include sprinting drills. If you're about to lift, include movement patterns you'll use.
5. **Don't fatigue**: Warmup should leave you energized, not tired

---

## CARDIO ACTIVATION (2-3 minutes)

Purpose: Elevate heart rate, body temperature, and blood flow to muscles.

| Exercise | Duration | Full Body Impact | Technique |
|----------|----------|------------------|-----------|
| **Jumping Jacks** | 30-60 sec | Elevates HR, mobilizes shoulders and hips | Feet together, arms at sides → jump feet wide, arms overhead → return. Continuous rhythm. Classic warmup exercise. |
| **High Knees** | 30 sec | Hip flexors, core, cardiovascular | Run in place driving knees toward chest. Pump arms. Stay on balls of feet. Higher knees = more hip flexor activation. |
| **Butt Kicks** | 30 sec | Hamstrings, cardiovascular | Run in place kicking heels toward glutes. Quick rhythm. Stretches quads dynamically. |
| **Jogging in Place** | 30-60 sec | General cardiovascular | Light jog with minimal impact. Good transition between exercises. |
| **Jump Rope (or Imaginary)** | 60-90 sec | Calves, shoulders, coordination, CV | Actual rope or mimicked motion. Excellent full-body warmup. Stay on balls of feet. |
| **Mountain Climbers** | 30 sec | Core, shoulders, hip flexors | Plank position, drive knees to chest alternately. High-intensity option. |
| **Seal Jacks** | 30 sec | Chest, shoulders (adds horizontal opening) | Like jumping jacks but arms go wide to sides (clapping in front). Opens chest. |
| **Star Jumps** | 30 sec | Explosive full body | Jump from squat to star shape (arms and legs spread), land in squat. More intense than jumping jacks. |

---

## DYNAMIC STRETCHING (3-4 minutes)

Purpose: Move joints through full range of motion, increase flexibility dynamically.

| Exercise | Duration/Reps | Primary Target | Technique |
|----------|---------------|----------------|-----------|
| **Arm Circles (Progressive)** | 15 forward, 15 backward | Shoulders, rotator cuff | Start small, progressively increase to large circles. Control the movement. |
| **Arm Swings (Cross-Body)** | 15 reps | Chest, shoulders, upper back | Swing arms across body horizontally, alternating which arm is on top. Opens chest and upper back. |
| **Leg Swings (Front-Back)** | 15 each leg | Hip flexors, hamstrings | Hold support, swing leg forward and backward with increasing range. |
| **Leg Swings (Side-to-Side)** | 15 each leg | Adductors, abductors | Swing leg across body and out to side. |
| **Hip Circles** | 10 each direction per leg | Hip joint | Standing on one leg, circle other leg in large controlled circles. |
| **Torso Twists** | 15 each side | Obliques, thoracic spine | Feet planted, rotate upper body side to side. Arms can swing freely or hands on hips. |
| **Neck Rolls (Gentle)** | 10 each direction | Neck, upper traps | Gentle half-circles (ear to shoulder to chest to other shoulder). Avoid rolling head backward (hyperextension). |
| **Wrist Circles** | 10 each direction | Wrists, forearms | Circle wrists in both directions. Essential if using hands for support/gripping. |

---

## MOVEMENT PREPARATION (2-3 minutes)

Purpose: Rehearse movement patterns, activate key muscles, prepare neuromuscular system.

| Exercise | Duration/Reps | Full Body Impact | Technique |
|----------|---------------|------------------|-----------|
| **Bodyweight Squats** | 15-20 reps | Lower body pattern, hip/knee/ankle mobility | Full depth squats with perfect form. Sit back, chest up, knees tracking over toes. |
| **Walk-Outs (Inchworms)** | 8-10 reps | Hamstrings, shoulders, core | From standing, fold over, walk hands to plank, walk back, stand. Do push-up at bottom for added challenge. |
| **World's Greatest Stretch** | 5 each side | Hip flexors, hamstrings, thoracic, adductors | Lunge position → elbow inside front foot → rotate and reach to ceiling → return. The best bang-for-buck stretch. |
| **Walking Knee Hugs** | 10 each leg | Glutes, hip flexors | Step forward, pull knee to chest with arms, release and step to next leg. Stretches glutes of hugged leg, hip flexors of standing leg. |
| **Walking Quad Stretch** | 10 each leg | Quads, hip flexors | Step forward, grab ankle behind you, pull heel to glute, slight lean forward. |
| **Lunges with Rotation** | 8 each side | Legs, core, thoracic spine | Forward lunge, rotate torso toward front leg, return, repeat other side. Multi-planar movement prep. |
| **Lateral Lunges** | 8 each side | Adductors, glutes | Step wide to side, shift weight, sit into hip, push back. |
| **Cat-Cow** | 10 reps | Spinal mobility | On all fours, alternate arching and rounding spine. |
| **Bird Dog** | 10 each side | Core, glutes | On all fours, extend opposite arm and leg. |
| **Toy Soldiers (Straight-Leg Kicks)** | 10 each leg | Hamstrings | Walk forward kicking straight leg to touch opposite hand. Dynamic hamstring stretch. |
| **Spiderman Steps** | 8 each side | Hip flexors, adductors | From standing, lunge forward deeply placing hands inside front foot, return. Opens hips comprehensively. |

---

## READY-TO-USE WARMUP ROUTINES

### 5-MINUTE QUICK WARMUP (Minimum Effective Dose)
For when time is very limited:

1. Jumping Jacks: 30 sec
2. Arm Circles: 15 each direction
3. Leg Swings (front-back): 10 each leg
4. Bodyweight Squats: 15 reps
5. Walk-Outs: 5 reps
6. Lunges with Rotation: 5 each side

### 10-MINUTE COMPLETE WARMUP (Gold Standard)
For optimal preparation:

**Minutes 1-2 (Cardio):**
- 30 sec jumping jacks
- 30 sec high knees
- 30 sec butt kicks
- 30 sec light jog

**Minutes 3-4 (Dynamic Stretching):**
- Arm circles: 10 each direction
- Arm swings: 10 reps
- Leg swings (both directions): 10 each leg
- Torso twists: 10 each side

**Minutes 5-6 (Movement Prep):**
- World's Greatest Stretch: 5 each side
- Walking knee hugs: 8 each leg

**Minutes 7-8 (Pattern Practice):**
- Bodyweight squats: 15 reps
- Walk-outs: 8 reps
- Lunges with rotation: 6 each side

**Minutes 9-10 (Specific):**
- Activity-specific movements
- Warmup sets if lifting

### 15-MINUTE COMPREHENSIVE WARMUP (Pre-Competition/Important Session)
For when performance matters most:

Add to 10-minute routine:
- Extended glute activation (bridges, clamshells)
- Extended hip mobility (pigeon, 90/90)
- Plyometric primers (jumping, bounding)
- Mental preparation/visualization

---

## KEY WARMUP PRINCIPLES SUMMARY

1. **Dynamic > Static pre-workout** — Save static stretching for after
2. **Progress from general to specific** — Cardio → stretching → movement patterns → activity-specific
3. **Match warmup to activity** — Leg day needs more hip work; throwing sports need more shoulder work
4. **Light sweat = ready** — A good indicator you've raised body temperature sufficiently
5. **5 minutes minimum, 10 minutes optimal** — Don't skip it, but don't overdo it either
6. **Warmup sets count** — Ramping up to working weight is part of the warmup
7. **Consistency matters** — A regular warmup routine becomes automatic and thorough
8. **Listen to your body** — Some days need more warmup than others

**Sources:**
- NSCA Essentials of Strength Training and Conditioning - Warmup protocols
- Behm & Chaouachi (2011) - "A Review of the Acute Effects of Static and Dynamic Stretching on Performance"
- Bishop (2003) - "Warm-Up I: Potential Mechanisms and the Effects of Passive Warm-Up on Exercise Performance"
- McMillian et al. (2006) - "Dynamic vs. Static-Stretching Warm Up"
- ACSM Guidelines for Exercise Testing and Prescription
```

---

# PART 2: ADD-ON PROGRAMS (Premium+)

## 2.1 Kegel / Pelvic Floor

**Query:** "List all kegel and pelvic floor exercises for both men and women with: name, description, duration/reps, difficulty, benefits. Include progressions from beginner to advanced."

**Response:**
```
COMPLETED BY CLAUDE

## WHAT ARE KEGELS?
- Exercises that strengthen pelvic floor muscles
- Developed by Dr. Arnold Kegel in 1940s
- Support bladder, bowel, and sexual organs
- Can be done anywhere, invisibly

## HOW TO FIND PELVIC FLOOR MUSCLES
- Imagine stopping urination mid-stream
- For men: Also retract penis inward / pull scrotum up
- For women: Also squeeze vagina like picking up a marble
- Should NOT feel it in glutes, thighs, or abs

## BEGINNER EXERCISES (Weeks 1-4)
| Exercise | Duration/Reps | Difficulty | Notes |
|----------|---------------|------------|-------|
| Quick Flicks | 10 reps (1-2 sec hold) | Beginner | Squeeze and release quickly |
| Basic Kegel Hold | 3-5 sec hold, 10 reps | Beginner | 3x per day |
| Elevator Kegel | 5 sec up, 5 sec down | Beginner | Gradually tighten in "floors" |
| Bridge with Kegel | 10 reps | Beginner | Add kegel at top of glute bridge |

## INTERMEDIATE EXERCISES (Weeks 5-8)
| Exercise | Duration/Reps | Difficulty | Notes |
|----------|---------------|------------|-------|
| Extended Hold | 5-10 sec hold, 10 reps | Intermediate | Progress hold time |
| Long + Short Combo | 10 long + 10 short | Intermediate | Endurance + power |
| Squat with Kegel | 10 reps | Intermediate | Engage pelvic floor during squat |
| Standing Kegels | 10 reps, 10 sec hold | Intermediate | Harder than lying down |

## ADVANCED EXERCISES (Weeks 9+)
| Exercise | Duration/Reps | Difficulty | Notes |
|----------|---------------|------------|-------|
| 10-Second Holds | 10 sec hold, 10 sec rest | Advanced | 10 reps, 3x daily |
| Weighted Kegels (Women) | Use vaginal weights | Advanced | 2x faster strength gains |
| Kegel + Core Combo | 10 reps | Advanced | Hollow hold + kegel |
| Pulsing Kegels | 20 quick pulses | Advanced | Rapid fire contractions |

## BENEFITS
**Both Sexes:** Bladder control, bowel control, core stability
**Men:** Prostate health, urinary control, sexual health, post-prostate surgery recovery
**Women:** Pregnancy support, easier delivery, postpartum recovery, pelvic organ prolapse prevention

## TRAINING PROTOCOL
- Weeks 1-2: 10 reps, 3-5 sec holds, 3x daily
- Weeks 3-4: 10 reps, 5-10 sec holds, 3x daily
- Goal: 30-40 Kegels per day spread throughout
- Results: 4-6 weeks for noticeable improvement

## CAUTIONS
- Don't do Kegels while urinating (damages bladder)
- Don't overdo it (can cause muscle tightness)
- Consult pelvic floor PT if issues persist
- 1/3 of people do them incorrectly - focus on isolation
```

```
COMPLETED - SEE DETAILED VERSION IN docs/research/RECOVERY.md

## POST-WORKOUT STATIC STRETCHES

### Upper Body Stretches
| Stretch | Muscles | Hold | Technique Tip |
|---------|---------|------|---------------|
| Chest Doorway Stretch | Pec major/minor | 30-60s | Elbow at 90°, step through |
| Cross-Body Shoulder | Posterior deltoid | 30s/side | Pull arm across body |
| Tricep Overhead | Triceps | 30s/side | Reach behind head |
| Bicep Wall Stretch | Biceps, anterior shoulder | 30s/side | Palm on wall, turn away |
| Neck Lateral Flexion | Traps, scalenes | 30s/side | Gentle head tilt |

### Lower Body Stretches
| Stretch | Muscles | Hold | Technique Tip |
|---------|---------|------|---------------|
| Standing Quad Stretch | Quadriceps | 30-60s/side | Keep knees together |
| Hamstring Stretch (Seated) | Hamstrings | 30-60s | Hinge at hips, flat back |
| Hip Flexor Lunge | Psoas, hip flexors | 60s/side | Tuck pelvis under |
| Pigeon Pose | Glutes, piriformis | 60-90s/side | Square hips |
| Calf Stretch (Wall) | Gastrocnemius | 30s/side | Heel down, straight leg |
| Butterfly Stretch | Adductors | 60s | Press knees down gently |

### Core/Back Stretches
| Stretch | Muscles | Hold | Technique Tip |
|---------|---------|------|---------------|
| Child's Pose | Lats, lower back | 60s | Reach arms forward |
| Cat-Cow | Spine (full) | 30s each | Slow, controlled |
| Supine Twist | Obliques, lower back | 30s/side | Shoulders flat |
| Cobra Stretch | Abs, hip flexors | 30s | Gentle extension only |

**General Tips:**
- Hold each stretch 30-60 seconds
- Breathe deeply into stretch
- Never bounce
- Stretch post-workout when muscles are warm
```

### Foam Rolling
**Query:** "List all foam rolling exercises by body part with: name, body part, technique description, duration, common mistakes to avoid."

**Response:**
```
COMPLETED - SEE DETAILED VERSION IN docs/research/RECOVERY.md

## FOAM ROLLING GUIDE

### Upper Body
| Body Part | Duration | Technique | Mistakes to Avoid |
|-----------|----------|-----------|-------------------|
| Lats | 60s/side | Lie on side, arm overhead, roll armpit to waist | Rolling too fast |
| Upper Back | 60-90s | Cross arms, support head, roll mid to upper back | Arching lower back |
| Pecs/Chest | 30-60s/side | Lie face down, foam roller at angle under chest | Too much pressure |

### Lower Body
| Body Part | Duration | Technique | Mistakes to Avoid |
|-----------|----------|-----------|-------------------|
| Quads | 60s/side | Face down, roller under thigh, roll hip to knee | Rolling over knee |
| Hamstrings | 60s/side | Sit on roller, roll glutes to knee | Not enough pressure |
| IT Band | 60-90s/side | Side-lying, roll hip to knee | Rolling directly on bone |
| Glutes | 60s/side | Sit on roller, cross one ankle over knee | Rolling spine |
| Calves | 60s/side | Sit with roller under calf, roll ankle to knee | Skipping soleus (bend knee) |
| Hip Flexors | 60s/side | Face down, roller at hip crease | Rolling into hip joint |
| Adductors | 60s/side | Face down, leg out to side on roller | Too fast |

### General Foam Rolling Guidelines
- Roll slowly (1-2 inches per second)
- Spend extra time on tight/tender spots (15-30s)
- Roll before workout (activation) and after (recovery)
- Avoid rolling directly on joints or bones
- Don't roll lower back directly (use ball or skip)
- 1-2 minutes per muscle group

**When to Foam Roll:**
- Before workout: 1-2 minutes/area for warm-up
- After workout: 2-3 minutes/area for recovery
- Rest days: Full body 15-20 minutes
```

---

## 2.5 Meditation & Breathing

### Breathing Exercises
**Query:** "List all breathing exercises for fitness/recovery with: name, technique description, duration, benefits, when to use (pre-workout/post-workout/sleep/stress)."

**Response:**
```
COMPLETED - SEE DETAILED VERSION IN docs/research/BREATHING-MEDITATION.md

## BREATHING EXERCISES

| Exercise | Technique | Duration | Benefits | When to Use |
|----------|-----------|----------|----------|-------------|
| **Box Breathing** | 4s inhale → 4s hold → 4s exhale → 4s hold | 4-10 min | Calms nervous system, focus | Pre-workout, stress, focus |
| **4-7-8 Breathing** | 4s inhale → 7s hold → 8s exhale | 4-8 cycles | Deep relaxation, sleep | Post-workout, sleep, anxiety |
| **Diaphragmatic Breathing** | Deep belly breaths, hand on belly rises | 5-10 min | Core activation, relaxation | Anytime, foundation |
| **Wim Hof Method** | 30 deep breaths → exhale hold → recovery breath | 3 rounds | Energy, cold tolerance | Pre-workout, morning |
| **Physiological Sigh** | Double inhale (nose) → long exhale (mouth) | 1-3 breaths | Instant calm | Stress, between sets |
| **Alternate Nostril** | Block one nostril, alternate breathing | 5-10 min | Balance, calm focus | Pre-meditation, stress |
| **Power Breathing** | Fast, forceful exhales | 30-60s | Energizing, warming | Pre-workout |

### Breathing by Situation
| Situation | Best Technique |
|-----------|----------------|
| Pre-workout energy | Wim Hof, Power Breathing |
| Post-workout recovery | Diaphragmatic, 4-7-8 |
| Between heavy sets | Physiological Sigh |
| Before sleep | 4-7-8 |
| Stress/anxiety | Box Breathing, Alternate Nostril |
| Focus/concentration | Box Breathing |
```

### Meditation Techniques

## MEDITATION TECHNIQUES

| Technique | Duration Options | Description | Benefits | Difficulty |
|-----------|------------------|-------------|----------|------------|
| **Mindfulness Meditation** | 5-30 min | Focus on breath, observe thoughts without judgment | Stress reduction, awareness | Beginner |
| **Body Scan** | 10-20 min | Progressive attention through body parts | Relaxation, body awareness, sleep | Beginner |
| **Guided Visualization** | 5-15 min | Follow guided imagery (success, calm place) | Motivation, anxiety relief | Beginner |
| **Loving-Kindness (Metta)** | 10-20 min | Send goodwill to self and others | Emotional wellbeing, compassion | Beginner |
| **Mantra Meditation** | 10-20 min | Repeat word/phrase (Om, peace, etc.) | Focus, calm | Beginner |
| **Walking Meditation** | 10-30 min | Mindful walking, focus on steps/breath | Active meditation, grounding | Beginner |
| **Visualization for Athletes** | 5-15 min | Mental rehearsal of movements/performance | Performance enhancement | Intermediate |
| **Breath Counting** | 5-15 min | Count breaths 1-10, restart | Focus training, beginner-friendly | Beginner |
| **Open Awareness** | 10-30 min | Observe all sensations without focus | Advanced mindfulness | Advanced |

|------|----------------|------|

| Post-workout recovery | Body scan, 4-7-8 breathing | After training |

| Motivation | Guided visualization | Morning |

## 2.6 Posture Correction

**Query:** "List all posture correction exercises for common issues (forward head, rounded shoulders, anterior pelvic tilt, etc.) with: postural issue, exercises to fix it, muscles to strengthen, muscles to stretch, daily routine."

**Response:**
```
COMPLETED - SEE DETAILED VERSION IN docs/research/POSTURE-BALANCE.md

## POSTURE CORRECTION GUIDE

### Forward Head Posture (Tech Neck)
| Category | Target |
|----------|--------|
| **Muscles to Strengthen** | Deep neck flexors, lower traps, rhomboids |
| **Muscles to Stretch** | Suboccipitals, SCM, pecs, upper traps |
| **Exercises** | Chin tucks (10x3 daily), Wall angels, Prone Y raises |
| **Daily Fix** | Set phone/screen at eye level, take breaks every 30 min |

### Rounded Shoulders (Kyphosis)
| Category | Target |
|----------|--------|
| **Muscles to Strengthen** | Rhomboids, middle/lower traps, rear delts, external rotators |
| **Muscles to Stretch** | Pecs, anterior deltoids, lats |
| **Exercises** | Face pulls, Band pull-aparts, Doorway stretch, Rows |
| **Daily Fix** | Chest stretches 3x daily, strengthen upper back |

### Anterior Pelvic Tilt (APT)
| Category | Target |
|----------|--------|
| **Muscles to Strengthen** | Glutes, abs (especially lower), hamstrings |
| **Muscles to Stretch** | Hip flexors (psoas, rectus femoris), lower back |
| **Exercises** | Glute bridges, Dead bugs, Hip flexor stretch, Planks |
| **Daily Fix** | Avoid excessive sitting, engage glutes when standing |

### Swayback Posture
| Category | Target |
|----------|--------|
| **Muscles to Strengthen** | Deep core, hip flexors, upper back |
| **Muscles to Stretch** | Hamstrings, chest |
| **Exercises** | Planks, Hip flexor strengthening, Wall slides |
| **Daily Fix** | Stand with weight over ankles, not forward |

### Daily Posture Routine (10 min)
| Exercise | Duration | Purpose |
|----------|----------|---------|
| Chin Tucks | 10 reps | Forward head |
| Wall Angels | 10 reps | Rounded shoulders |
| Doorway Stretch | 30s/side | Chest opening |
| Hip Flexor Stretch | 60s/side | APT |
| Glute Bridge | 15 reps | Glute activation |
| Dead Bug | 10/side | Core stability |
```

|------|-------|------|
| 1-2 | Static single-leg (eyes open) | 30s/leg |
| 3-4 | Static single-leg (eyes closed) | 30s/leg |
| 5-6 | Unstable surface (pillow, BOSU) | 30s/leg |
| 7-8 | Dynamic movements (reaches, catches) | 60s total |
| 9+ | Sport-specific, weighted, reactive | Progress |
```

**FITNESS NOTES:**
- Chicken breast and turkey are the leanest protein sources
- Beef liver is extremely high in Vitamin A (16,899 IU/100g) and B12 (59.3mcg/100g)
- Ground meats: always ask for lean (قليل الدهن) - fat content varies greatly
- Remove visible fat and skin when cutting for fat loss goals
- Lamb is fattier than beef on average - account for in macros
- Organ meats are nutrient-dense but should be limited to 1-2x/week due to high cholesterol/vitamin A

**Sources:** USDA FoodData Central, Egyptian Food Composition Tables

|-------------|--------------|----------|---------|-------|-----|-------|
| فسيخ | Fermented Mullet | 143 | 22g | 0g | 6g | ⚠️ Very high sodium (Sham El-Nessim) |
| ملوحة | Salted Fish | 148 | 24g | 0g | 5g | ⚠️ High sodium - limit intake |
| رنجة | Smoked Herring | 203 | 23g | 0g | 12g | Sham El-Nessim tradition |
| سردين مملح | Salted Sardines | 208 | 25g | 0g | 11g | High sodium |

**OMEGA-3 CONTENT (per 100g):**
| Fish | Omega-3 (EPA+DHA) |
|------|-------------------|
| Salmon | 2.3g |
| Sardines | 1.5g |
| Mackerel | 1.0g |
| Tuna (fresh) | 0.7g |
| Sea Bass | 0.6g |
| Tilapia | 0.2g |

**FITNESS NOTES:**
- Shrimp and white fish (tilapia, sole) = lowest calorie protein sources
- Fatty fish (salmon, mackerel, sardines) = best omega-3 sources (eat 2-3x/week)
- Avoid breaded/fried preparations - add 100-150 cal per serving
- Canned tuna in water = budget-friendly, high-protein option
- ⚠️ Fesikh/Moluha: Extremely high sodium - avoid during cutting phases
- Mercury concern: Limit large fish (tuna, swordfish) to 2-3 servings/week

**Sources:** USDA FoodData Central, FAO Fish Nutrition Data
```

- Soak dry legumes 8-12 hours (reduces cooking time + gas)
- Rinse canned legumes to reduce sodium by ~40%
- Combine legumes with grains (rice + lentils) for complete protein
- Add cumin/caraway to reduce digestive discomfort

**FITNESS NOTES:**
- Legumes = excellent budget protein for vegetarians
- High fiber content aids satiety during cutting
- Complete protein when combined with grains
- Edamame/soy = closest to animal protein quality
- Ful medames = Egyptian breakfast of champions (cheap, filling, high protein)

## 3.2 Carbohydrates

### Bread & Grains

**Response:**
```
COMPLETED BY CLAUDE (DETAILED VERSION)

## BREADS & GRAINS - COMPREHENSIVE DATABASE

### Egyptian Breads (عيش - Aish)

| Arabic Name | English Name | Cal/piece | Protein | Carbs | Fat | Fiber | Notes |
|-------------|--------------|-----------|---------|-------|-----|-------|-------|
| عيش بلدي | Baladi Bread (1 round, 80g) | 210 | 7g | 43g | 1g | 3g | Whole wheat, subsidized |

**GLYCEMIC INDEX GUIDE:**
| Category | GI Range | Examples |
|----------|----------|----------|
| Low GI | <55 | Brown rice, freekeh, bulgur, barley, oats |
| Medium GI | 56-69 | Basmati rice, couscous |
| High GI | >70 | White rice, white bread, instant noodles |

**FITNESS RECOMMENDATIONS:**
| Goal | Best Choices |
|------|--------------|
| Fat Loss | Freekeh, bulgur, brown rice, oats (low GI, high fiber) |
| Muscle Gain | Quinoa, freekeh (higher protein), any rice |
| Pre-Workout | White rice, aish baladi (fast energy) |
| Post-Workout | Any grain + protein source |
| Budget | White rice, oats, aish baladi (subsidized) |

**PORTION GUIDE (Cooked):**
- 1 cup cooked rice = ~200 cal
- 1 cup cooked pasta = ~220 cal
- 1 cup cooked oatmeal = ~150 cal
- 1 aish baladi = ~210 cal

**Sources:** USDA FoodData Central, Egyptian Food Composition Tables

### Homemade vs Restaurant Comparison

| Dish | Homemade (healthy) | Restaurant/Street | Difference |
|------|-------------------|-------------------|------------|
| Koshari | 450 cal | 650+ cal | More oil, larger portion |
| Macarona Bechamel | 380 cal | 550+ cal | Extra butter, cheese |
| Rice w/ Vermicelli | 250 cal | 350+ cal | More ghee |

**MACRO-FRIENDLY MODIFICATIONS:**
| Original | Modification | Calorie Savings |
|----------|--------------|-----------------|
| Regular pasta | Lentil/protein pasta | Same cal, +6g protein |
| White rice | Brown/basmati rice | Same cal, lower GI |
| Macarona bechamel | Light bechamel (skim milk) | -100 cal |
| Koshari | Extra lentils, less pasta | +5g protein |
| Rice w/ vermicelli | Skip vermicelli | -50 cal |

**PORTION AWARENESS:**
- Restaurant koshari = often 600-800 calories (double homemade)
- Pasta dishes: ask for no extra oil
- Rice dishes: standard cup = ~200 cal, restaurant portions = 1.5-2 cups

**Sources:** Egyptian Food Composition Tables, USDA, Restaurant Analysis
```

| Fruit | Sugar/100g |
|-------|------------|

| 🥉 Cantaloupe | 8g |
| Grapefruit | 7g |
| Peach | 8g |

| Fruit | Sugar/100g |
|-------|------------|

| Grapes | 16g |
| Mango | 14g |
| Banana | 12g |
| Pomegranate | 14g |

### Pre/Post Workout Fruit Guide

| Timing | Best Fruits | Why |
|--------|-------------|-----|
| Pre-Workout (30-60min) | Banana, dates, apple | Fast digesting carbs |
| Post-Workout | Banana, mango, watermelon | Glycogen replenishment |
| Fat Loss Snack | Strawberry, grapefruit, watermelon | Low calorie, filling |
| Bulking Snack | Banana, dates, mango | Calorie-dense |

**PORTION GUIDE:**
| Fruit | Serving | Calories |
|-------|---------|----------|
| 1 medium banana | 120g | 105 cal |
| 1 medium apple | 180g | 95 cal |
| 1 medium orange | 130g | 60 cal |
| 1 cup watermelon | 150g | 45 cal |
| 2 medium dates | 40g | 110 cal |
| 1 cup grapes | 150g | 105 cal |

### Healthy Fat Sources (Beyond Oils)

| Food | Serving | Calories | Fat | Type |
|------|---------|----------|-----|------|
| Avocado | 1/2 fruit | 120 | 11g | Monounsaturated |
| Almonds | 23 nuts (28g) | 164 | 14g | Monounsaturated |
| Walnuts | 14 halves (28g) | 185 | 18g | Omega-3 (ALA) |
| Flaxseeds | 1 tbsp | 37 | 3g | Omega-3 (ALA) |
| Chia Seeds | 1 tbsp | 58 | 4g | Omega-3 |
| Olives | 10 medium | 40 | 4g | Monounsaturated |
| Dark Chocolate (85%) | 30g | 170 | 14g | Saturated |

### Oil Comparison for Fitness

| Goal | Best Oils | Avoid |
|------|-----------|-------|
| Heart Health | Olive oil, avocado oil | Palm oil, hydrogenated |
| High-Heat Cooking | Ghee, avocado oil | EVOO (burns) |
| Omega-3 Intake | Fish oil, flax oil | N/A |
| Calorie Control | Cooking spray, measure all oils | Unmeasured pours |
| Muscle Building | Any - focus on hitting fat macros | Trans fats |

### Hidden Fats Warning

| Food | Hidden Fat Source | Calories Added |
|------|-------------------|----------------|
| Restaurant rice | Extra ghee | +50-100 cal |
| Fried foods | Absorbed oil | +100-200 cal |
| Koshari sauce | Oil in tomato sauce | +30-50 cal |
| Salad (dressed) | Oil/mayo | +100-200 cal |
| Falafel | Deep fried | +100 cal vs baked |

**MEASURING TIPS:**
- 1 tablespoon oil = 120 calories (easy to pour 3x this)
- Use measuring spoons or spray
- 1 second spray = ~10 calories
- Restaurants use 2-3x more oil than needed

**DAILY FAT TARGETS:**
| Goal | Fat (% of calories) | Example (2000 cal) |
|------|---------------------|-------------------|
| General Health | 25-35% | 55-78g |
| Fat Loss | 20-30% | 44-67g |
| Keto/Low-Carb | 70-75% | 155-167g |
| Muscle Building | 25-30% | 55-67g |

**Sources:** USDA FoodData Central, Smoke Point Research
```

| Fattah | Garlic, cumin, vinegar |

**FITNESS NOTES:**
- Spices are virtually calorie-free - use generously for flavor
- Capsaicin (chili) may slightly boost metabolism
- Turmeric + black pepper = 2000% better absorption
- Salt: limit to 2,300mg/day (1 tsp) - most Egyptians exceed this
- Fresh herbs > dried for antioxidants

### Macro-Optimized Breakfast Ideas

**FOR FAT LOSS (400 cal, 30g protein):**
- 3 egg whites + 1 whole egg scrambled
- 100g ful (no oil added)
- Salad (unlimited)
- Skip the bread
= 380 cal, 32g protein

**FOR MUSCLE GAIN (600 cal, 40g protein):**
- 2 whole eggs + 2 whites
- 150g ful
- 1 aish baladi
- 100g Greek yogurt
= 590 cal, 42g protein

**QUICK PROTEIN BREAKFAST:**
- 200g Greek yogurt 0%
- 30g protein powder
- 1 banana
= 350 cal, 45g protein

**Sources:** Egyptian Food Analysis, USDA, Restaurant Portions

| تكة | Tikka | 100g | 160 | 22 | 7 |

**Fitness-Friendly Street Food Choices:**
1. **Best for Muscle Building:** Shish Tawook, Kebab, Tikka (high protein, low carb)
2. **Best for Fat Loss:** Baked Ta'ameya, Grilled meats without bread
3. **Best Post-Workout:** Koshari (high carb), Hawawshi (carb + protein)
4. **Avoid when cutting:** Fiteer (very high calorie), fried items

**Healthier Ordering Tips:**
- Ask for grilled (meshwi) instead of fried (ma'li)
- Request less oil in ful
- Choose baked ta'ameya when available
- Skip the fried onions on koshari to save 100+ calories

**Sources:** Egyptian Food Composition Tables, Restaurant Analysis
```

|-------------|--------------|--------------|-----------------|--------------|-----------|
| أم علي | Om Ali | 280 | 560 | 1 bowl (200g) | 36 |
| أم علي بالمكسرات | Om Ali (with nuts) | 320 | 640 | 1 bowl (200g) | 32 |
| رز باللبن | Roz bil Laban (Rice Pudding) | 135 | 243 | 1 cup (180g) | 25 |
| رز باللبن بالقشطة | Rice Pudding (with cream) | 170 | 306 | 1 cup (180g) | 27 |
| مهلبية | Mahalabeya | 120 | 180 | 1 bowl (150g) | 18 |
| سحلب | Sahlab | 125 | 250 | 1 cup (200g) | 30 |
| عيش السرايا | Aish El Saraya | 350 | 525 | 150g | 45 |

### Ice Cream & Frozen (per 100g)

| Arabic Name | English Name | Calories | Protein (g) | Carbs (g) | Fat (g) |
|-------------|--------------|----------|-------------|-----------|---------|
| آيس كريم فانيليا | Vanilla Ice Cream | 207 | 3.5 | 24 | 11 |
| آيس كريم شوكولاتة | Chocolate Ice Cream | 216 | 3.8 | 28 | 11 |
| دوندرما | Dondurma (stretchy) | 180 | 3 | 28 | 6 |
| سوربيه فواكه | Fruit Sorbet | 97 | 0.5 | 25 | 0.1 |
| فروزن يوجرت | Frozen Yogurt | 127 | 3 | 23 | 3 |

**Fitness Considerations:**
- Egyptian desserts are very high in sugar and calories
- Best enjoyed occasionally, not daily
- If bulking: Om Ali provides calories + some protein
- If cutting: Fruit sorbet or small portion of rice pudding (lowest cal)
- Ramadan tip: Limit to 1 small piece of sweets after iftar

**Lower-Calorie Alternatives:**
- Roz bil Laban made with skim milk
- Fresh fruit instead of syrup-based sweets
- Small portion of mahalabeya (lower calorie pudding)

**Sources:** Egyptian Food Composition Tables, USDA FoodData Central
```

| Arabic Name | English Name | Calories | Carbs (g) | Sugar (g) | Notes |
|-------------|--------------|----------|-----------|-----------|-------|
| كركديه | Karkade (sweetened) | 95 | 24 | 24 | Lowers blood pressure |
| كركديه بدون سكر | Karkade (no sugar) | 10 | 2 | 0 | Zero calorie option |
| تمر هندي | Tamr Hindi (Tamarind) | 130 | 33 | 30 | Ramadan favorite |
| قمر الدين | Qamar El Din (Apricot) | 150 | 38 | 35 | Ramadan traditional |
| سوبيا | Sobia (Coconut) | 220 | 42 | 40 | High calorie |
| عرقسوس | Irqsous (Licorice) | 100 | 24 | 22 | Traditional |
| عصير قصب | Aseer Asab (Sugarcane) | 180 | 45 | 42 | Street drink, very sweet |
| دوم | Doum (Palm Fruit) | 100 | 25 | 22 | Traditional |

| عصير أفوكادو | Avocado Shake | 220 | 25 | 18 | With milk, healthy fats |
| عصير موز | Banana Shake | 175 | 35 | 25 | With milk |

### Commercial Beverages (per 330ml)

| Beverage | Calories | Sugar (g) | Recommendation |
|----------|----------|-----------|----------------|
| Cola (regular) | 139 | 35 | Avoid - empty calories |
| Cola (diet) | 1 | 0 | Better but artificial sweeteners |
| Sprite/7Up | 140 | 36 | Avoid |
| Fanta | 150 | 39 | Avoid - highest sugar |
| Energy drink | 165 | 40 | Occasional only |
| Sports drink | 80 | 21 | Post-workout only |

## BEVERAGE RECOMMENDATIONS BY GOAL

| Goal | Best Choices | Limit/Avoid |
|------|--------------|-------------|
| Fat Loss | Water, unsweetened tea, black coffee, karkade (no sugar) | Juices, sodas, sahlab, sweetened drinks |
| Muscle Building | Milk, protein shakes, water, banana shake | Sodas, excessive caffeine |
| General Health | Water, hibiscus (no sugar), green tea, ginger | Sweetened drinks, sodas |
| Pre-Workout | Black coffee, green tea | Heavy drinks, sahlab |
| Post-Workout | Water, milk, diluted juice | Carbonated drinks |
| Hydration | Water, electrolyte drinks, diluted lemon | High caffeine, alcohol |

**Egyptian Beverage Calorie Traps:**
- Traditional tea with 3+ sugars = 70+ calories per cup
- Sahlab = 250 calories (like a small meal)
- Fresh juices often have added sugar
- Ramadan drinks (qamar el din, tamr hindi) are very high sugar

**Zero/Low Calorie Options:**
- Plain tea or coffee
- Karkade without sugar
- Water with lemon
- Mint tea
- Unsweetened herbal teas

**Sources:** Egyptian Food Composition Tables, USDA FoodData Central
```

- Adjustable dumbbells (up to 25kg each)
- Adjustable bench
- Pull-up bar

**Option B - Barbell Focus (~$300-500):**
- Olympic barbell + 60kg plates
- Squat stands
- Flat bench
- Pull-up bar

|------------|---------------|-------------|
| Dumbbells only | 2x2m | 3x3m |
| Dumbbells + Bench | 2.5x2m | 3x3m |
| Barbell setup | 3x3m | 4x3m |

| Stage | Budget | Add Equipment | New Capabilities |
|-------|--------|---------------|------------------|
| Stage 1 | $0 | Bodyweight only | 70% of exercises |
| Stage 2 | $50 | Pull-up bar, bands | 80% of exercises |

# PART 5: WORKOUT PROGRAMS

## 5.1 Beginner Programs

**Query:** "Create a detailed 4-week beginner full body workout program for someone with no experience. Include: weekly schedule, exercises per day, sets, reps, rest times, progression each week."

**Response:**
```
COMPLETED - SEE DETAILED VERSION IN docs/research/WORKOUT-PROGRAMS.md

## BEGINNER FULL BODY PROGRAM (4 Weeks)

### Weekly Schedule
| Day | Workout |
|-----|---------|
| Monday | Full Body A |
| Tuesday | Rest |
| Wednesday | Full Body B |
| Thursday | Rest |
| Friday | Full Body A |
| Saturday | Rest |
| Sunday | Rest |

*Week 2 alternates to B-A-B. Continue alternating.*

### Full Body Workout A

| Exercise | Sets | Reps | Rest | Notes |
|----------|------|------|------|-------|
| Barbell Back Squat | 3 | 8-10 | 90-120s | Primary leg compound |
| Flat Barbell Bench Press | 3 | 8-10 | 90-120s | Primary chest compound |
| Bent Over Barbell Row | 3 | 8-10 | 90-120s | Primary back compound |
| Overhead Dumbbell Press | 2 | 10-12 | 60-90s | Shoulder development |
| Romanian Deadlift | 2 | 10-12 | 90s | Posterior chain |
| Dumbbell Bicep Curl | 2 | 12-15 | 60s | Arm isolation |
| Tricep Rope Pushdown | 2 | 12-15 | 60s | Arm isolation |
| Plank | 3 | 30-45s | 45s | Core stability |

### Full Body Workout B

| Exercise | Sets | Reps | Rest | Notes |
|----------|------|------|------|-------|
| Leg Press | 3 | 10-12 | 90s | Quad-focused |
| Incline Dumbbell Press | 3 | 8-10 | 90s | Upper chest emphasis |
| Lat Pulldown | 3 | 10-12 | 90s | Back width |
| Dumbbell Lateral Raise | 2 | 12-15 | 60s | Shoulder width |
| Leg Curl | 2 | 12-15 | 60s | Hamstring isolation |
| Hammer Curl | 2 | 12-15 | 60s | Brachialis & forearms |
| Overhead Tricep Extension | 2 | 12-15 | 60s | Long head tricep |
| Cable Crunch | 3 | 15-20 | 45s | Weighted ab work |

### 4-Week Progression

| Week | Focus | RPE | Weight Change |
|------|-------|-----|---------------|
| Week 1 | Learn form | 6-7 | Start light |
| Week 2 | Add reps | 7 | Same weight |
| Week 3 | Add weight | 7-8 | +5 lbs compounds, +2.5 lbs isolation |
| Week 4 | Peak then deload | 8 → 6 | Push day 1-2, reduce 20% day 3 |

**Sources:** NSCA guidelines, research-backed progression models
```

## 5.2 PPL (Push Pull Legs)

**Query:** "Create a detailed PPL (Push Pull Legs) workout program. Include: weekly schedule, all exercises for each day, sets, reps, rest times, when to increase weight."

**Response:**
```
COMPLETED - SEE DETAILED VERSION IN docs/research/WORKOUT-PROGRAMS.md

## PPL - PUSH PULL LEGS (6-Day Split)

### Weekly Schedule
| Day | Workout | Focus |
|-----|---------|-------|
| Monday | Push A | Chest, Shoulders, Triceps (Strength) |
| Tuesday | Pull A | Back, Biceps, Rear Delts (Strength) |
| Wednesday | Legs A | Quads, Hamstrings, Calves (Strength) |
| Thursday | Push B | Chest, Shoulders, Triceps (Hypertrophy) |
| Friday | Pull B | Back, Biceps, Rear Delts (Hypertrophy) |
| Saturday | Legs B | Quads, Hamstrings, Calves (Hypertrophy) |
| Sunday | Rest | Complete recovery |

### Push A (Strength Focus)
| Exercise | Sets | Reps | Rest |
|----------|------|------|------|
| Barbell Bench Press | 4 | 4-6 | 3-4min |
| Overhead Press | 4 | 4-6 | 3-4min |
| Incline Dumbbell Press | 3 | 6-8 | 2-3min |
| Dumbbell Lateral Raise | 3 | 10-12 | 60-90s |
| Tricep Dips | 3 | 6-8 | 2min |
| Overhead Tricep Extension | 3 | 8-10 | 60-90s |

### Pull A (Strength Focus)
| Exercise | Sets | Reps | Rest |
|----------|------|------|------|
| Barbell Deadlift | 4 | 4-6 | 3-5min |
| Weighted Pull-Ups | 4 | 4-6 | 3min |
| Barbell Row | 3 | 6-8 | 2-3min |
| Face Pulls | 3 | 12-15 | 60s |
| Barbell Curl | 3 | 6-8 | 90s |
| Hammer Curl | 3 | 8-10 | 60s |

### Legs A (Strength Focus)
| Exercise | Sets | Reps | Rest |
|----------|------|------|------|
| Barbell Back Squat | 4 | 4-6 | 3-5min |
| Romanian Deadlift | 3 | 6-8 | 2-3min |
| Leg Press | 3 | 8-10 | 2min |
| Leg Curl | 3 | 8-10 | 90s |
| Standing Calf Raise | 4 | 10-12 | 60s |

### Push B (Hypertrophy Focus)
| Exercise | Sets | Reps | Rest |
|----------|------|------|------|
| Incline Barbell Press | 4 | 8-10 | 90-120s |
| Dumbbell Shoulder Press | 3 | 10-12 | 90s |
| Cable Fly | 3 | 12-15 | 60s |
| Lateral Raise | 4 | 12-15 | 45s |
| Rope Pushdown | 3 | 12-15 | 60s |
| Skull Crushers | 3 | 10-12 | 60s |

### Pull B (Hypertrophy Focus)
| Exercise | Sets | Reps | Rest |
|----------|------|------|------|
| Lat Pulldown | 4 | 10-12 | 90s |
| Seated Cable Row | 4 | 10-12 | 90s |
| Dumbbell Row | 3 | 10-12 | 60s |
| Rear Delt Fly | 4 | 12-15 | 45s |
| Incline Dumbbell Curl | 3 | 12-15 | 60s |
| Cable Curl | 3 | 12-15 | 45s |

### Legs B (Hypertrophy Focus)
| Exercise | Sets | Reps | Rest |
|----------|------|------|------|
| Leg Press | 4 | 10-12 | 90s |
| Walking Lunges | 3 | 12/leg | 90s |
| Leg Extension | 3 | 12-15 | 60s |
| Lying Leg Curl | 4 | 10-12 | 60s |
| Seated Calf Raise | 4 | 15-20 | 45s |

### Progression: Two-for-Two Rule
1. Hit top of rep range on last set for 2 consecutive workouts
2. Increase weight: +5 lbs upper body, +10 lbs lower body
3. Reset to bottom of rep range with new weight

**Sources:** PPL research, RP Strength recommendations
```

---

## 5.3 Upper/Lower Split

**Query:** "Create a detailed Upper/Lower split workout program (4 days). Include: weekly schedule, all exercises, sets, reps, rest times, progression model."

**Response:**
```
COMPLETED - SEE DETAILED VERSION IN docs/research/WORKOUT-PROGRAMS.md

## UPPER/LOWER SPLIT (4 Days)

### Weekly Schedule
| Day | Workout |
|-----|---------|
| Monday | Upper A (Strength) |
| Tuesday | Lower A (Strength) |
| Wednesday | Rest |
| Thursday | Upper B (Hypertrophy) |
| Friday | Lower B (Hypertrophy) |
| Saturday | Rest |
| Sunday | Rest |

### Upper A (Strength Focus)
| Exercise | Sets | Reps | Rest |
|----------|------|------|------|
| Barbell Bench Press | 4 | 4-6 | 3min |
| Barbell Row | 4 | 4-6 | 3min |
| Overhead Press | 3 | 6-8 | 2min |
| Weighted Pull-Ups | 3 | 6-8 | 2min |
| Barbell Curl | 2 | 8-10 | 90s |
| Skull Crushers | 2 | 8-10 | 90s |
| Face Pulls | 3 | 15-20 | 60s |

### Lower A (Strength Focus)
| Exercise | Sets | Reps | Rest |
|----------|------|------|------|
| Barbell Back Squat | 4 | 4-6 | 3-4min |
| Romanian Deadlift | 4 | 6-8 | 2-3min |
| Leg Press | 3 | 8-10 | 2min |
| Leg Curl | 3 | 8-10 | 90s |
| Standing Calf Raise | 4 | 10-12 | 60s |
| Hanging Leg Raise | 3 | 10-15 | 60s |

### Upper B (Hypertrophy Focus)
| Exercise | Sets | Reps | Rest |
|----------|------|------|------|
| Incline Dumbbell Press | 3 | 8-12 | 90s |
| Lat Pulldown | 3 | 10-12 | 90s |
| Dumbbell Shoulder Press | 3 | 10-12 | 90s |
| Seated Cable Row | 3 | 10-12 | 90s |
| Lateral Raise | 3 | 12-15 | 60s |
| Incline Curl | 3 | 12-15 | 60s |
| Tricep Pushdown | 3 | 12-15 | 60s |
| Rear Delt Fly | 3 | 15-20 | 45s |

### Lower B (Hypertrophy Focus)
| Exercise | Sets | Reps | Rest |
|----------|------|------|------|
| Leg Press | 4 | 10-12 | 90s |
| Goblet Squat or Lunges | 3 | 12-15 | 90s |
| Leg Extension | 3 | 12-15 | 60s |
| Lying Leg Curl | 3 | 12-15 | 60s |
| Hip Thrust | 3 | 10-12 | 90s |
| Seated Calf Raise | 4 | 15-20 | 45s |
| Cable Crunch | 3 | 15-20 | 45s |

### Progression Model
- Strength days: Add 5 lbs when completing all sets at top of rep range
- Hypertrophy days: Add 2.5-5 lbs when completing all sets at top of rep range
- Deload every 4-6 weeks (reduce volume 40-50%)

**Why Upper/Lower Works:**
- 4 days/week - sustainable for most schedules
- Each muscle trained 2×/week
- Balance of strength and hypertrophy
- Adequate recovery between sessions

**Sources:** NSCA guidelines, Lyle McDonald's Generic Bulking Routine
```
