## 5.4 Home Workout Programs

**Query:** "Create a detailed home workout program with no equipment (bodyweight only) for building muscle. Include: weekly schedule, exercises, sets, reps, progressions, how to make exercises harder over time."

**Response:**
```
COMPLETED - SEE DETAILED VERSION IN docs/research/WORKOUT-PROGRAMS.md

## HOME/BODYWEIGHT PROGRAM

### Weekly Schedule
| Day | Workout |
|-----|---------|
| Monday | Push Day |
| Tuesday | Pull Day |
| Wednesday | Rest or Cardio |
| Thursday | Legs Day |
| Friday | Upper Body (Full) |
| Saturday | Core & Cardio |
| Sunday | Rest |

### Push Day (Chest, Shoulders, Triceps)
| Exercise | Sets | Reps | Progression |
|----------|------|------|-------------|
| Push-Ups | 4 | 15-25 | → Diamond → Decline → Archer |
| Pike Push-Ups | 3 | 10-15 | → Elevated Pike → Wall Handstand |
| Diamond Push-Ups | 3 | 10-15 | → Close-Grip Decline |
| Dips (using chairs) | 3 | 8-15 | → Weighted (backpack) |
| Plank Shoulder Taps | 3 | 10/side | → Slower tempo |

### Pull Day (Back, Biceps)
| Exercise | Sets | Reps | Progression |
|----------|------|------|-------------|
| Pull-Ups/Chin-Ups | 4 | 5-12 | → Wide → L-Sit → Archer |
| Inverted Rows | 4 | 10-15 | → Feet elevated → Single-arm |
| Doorway Curls | 3 | 10-15 | → Slower eccentric |
| Back Extensions | 3 | 15-20 | → Superman holds |
| Australian Pull-Ups | 3 | 10-15 | → Single-arm |

### Legs Day (Quads, Hamstrings, Glutes)
| Exercise | Sets | Reps | Progression |
|----------|------|------|-------------|
| Squat | 4 | 15-25 | → Jump Squat → Pistol Squat |
| Bulgarian Split Squat | 3 | 10-15/leg | → Weighted (backpack) |
| Romanian Deadlift (single-leg) | 3 | 10-12/leg | → Add backpack weight |
| Glute Bridge | 3 | 15-20 | → Single-leg → Elevated |
| Calf Raise | 4 | 20-30 | → Single-leg → Deficit |
| Wall Sit | 3 | 30-60s | → Single-leg |

### Upper Body (Full)
| Exercise | Sets | Reps |
|----------|------|------|
| Push-Up Variation | 3 | To failure |
| Pull-Up Variation | 3 | To failure |
| Pike Push-Up | 3 | 10-15 |
| Inverted Row | 3 | 10-15 |
| Dips | 3 | 8-15 |
| Plank | 3 | 45-60s |

### Core & Cardio Day
| Exercise | Sets | Reps/Time |
|----------|------|-----------|
| Plank | 3 | 45-60s |
| Mountain Climbers | 3 | 30s |
| Bicycle Crunches | 3 | 20/side |
| Leg Raises | 3 | 15-20 |
| Burpees | 3 | 10-15 |
| Jump Squats | 3 | 15-20 |

### Progression Methods (No Equipment)
1. **Add reps** until you reach 25-30
2. **Add sets** (one extra set per week)
3. **Harder variation** (see progression column)
4. **Slower tempo** (4 seconds down, 2 up)
5. **Reduced rest** (60s → 45s → 30s)
6. **Add weight** (backpack with books)
7. **One-limb variations** (single-leg, single-arm)

**Sources:** Calisthenics research, bodyweight training guides
```

---

## 5.5 Fat Loss Programs

**Query:** "Create a detailed fat loss workout program combining resistance training and cardio. Include: weekly schedule, exercises, HIIT protocols, cardio recommendations, rest days."

**Response:**
```
COMPLETED - SEE DETAILED VERSION IN docs/research/WORKOUT-PROGRAMS.md

## FAT LOSS PROGRAM

### Weekly Schedule
| Day | Workout | Duration |
|-----|---------|----------|
| Monday | Full Body Resistance + HIIT | 60 min |
| Tuesday | LISS Cardio or Active Recovery | 30-45 min |
| Wednesday | Full Body Resistance + Core | 50 min |
| Thursday | HIIT Only | 25-30 min |
| Friday | Full Body Resistance + HIIT | 60 min |
| Saturday | LISS Cardio | 45-60 min |
| Sunday | Complete Rest | - |

### Full Body Resistance (Circuit Style)
*Perform 3-4 rounds with minimal rest between exercises*

| Exercise | Reps | Notes |
|----------|------|-------|
| Goblet Squat | 12-15 | Keep tempo controlled |
| Push-Ups | 12-15 | Modify as needed |
| Dumbbell Row | 12/arm | Alternate arms |
| Reverse Lunge | 10/leg | Bodyweight or weighted |
| Dumbbell Shoulder Press | 12 | Standing for core engagement |
| Romanian Deadlift | 12 | Feel hamstring stretch |
| Plank | 30-45s | End of each circuit |

**Rest:** 15-30s between exercises, 90-120s between rounds

### HIIT Protocol Options

**Option A: Tabata (4 minutes)**
- 20 seconds work, 10 seconds rest
- 8 rounds
- Choose: Burpees, Jump Squats, Mountain Climbers, or Sprints

**Option B: 30/30 Intervals (15-20 minutes)**
- 30 seconds work, 30 seconds rest
- 15-20 rounds
- Alternate between 2-3 exercises

**Option C: EMOM - Every Minute on the Minute (20 minutes)**
- Minute 1: 15 Kettlebell Swings
- Minute 2: 10 Burpees
- Minute 3: 20 Mountain Climbers
- Minute 4: Rest
- Repeat 5 rounds

### LISS Cardio Options
| Activity | Duration | Target Heart Rate |
|----------|----------|-------------------|
| Walking (brisk) | 45-60 min | 50-65% max HR |
| Cycling | 30-45 min | 60-70% max HR |
| Swimming | 30-45 min | 60-70% max HR |
| Incline Treadmill Walking | 30-45 min | 55-65% max HR |
| Elliptical | 30-45 min | 60-70% max HR |

### Calorie Burn Estimates (per hour)
| Activity | 60kg Person | 80kg Person |
|----------|-------------|-------------|
| HIIT | 400-600 | 500-800 |
| Weight Training | 250-400 | 350-500 |
| Brisk Walking | 250-300 | 350-400 |
| Running (8 km/h) | 400-500 | 550-650 |
| Cycling (moderate) | 300-400 | 400-550 |

### Fat Loss Principles
1. **Caloric deficit is #1** - Training enhances deficit, doesn't replace it
2. **Prioritize resistance training** - Preserves muscle during fat loss
3. **HIIT for efficiency** - Burns calories in less time
4. **LISS for recovery** - Aids fat loss without taxing recovery
5. **Progressive overload** - Still increase weight/reps even in deficit
6. **Higher protein** - 1.6-2.2g/kg bodyweight to preserve muscle

**Nutrition Reminder:** Fat loss = 80% diet, 20% exercise

**Sources:** ACSM fat loss guidelines, research on resistance training during deficit
```

---

```
| Bulgarian Split Squat | 3 | 10/leg |
| Jump Squat | 3 | 10 |
| Calf Raise | 3 | 20 |

### Progression Rule
Move to next level when you can complete target reps with perfect form for 2 consecutive sessions.

**Sources:** Overcoming Gravity, calisthenics research, gymnastics strength training
```

# PART 6: NUTRITION GUIDELINES

## 6.1 Calorie Calculations

**Query:** "Explain all methods to calculate daily calorie needs (TDEE) with formulas. Include: BMR formulas (Mifflin-St Jeor, Harris-Benedict), activity multipliers, adjustments for goals (fat loss/muscle gain/maintenance)."

**Response:**
```
COMPLETED - SEE DETAILED VERSION IN docs/research/NUTRITION.md

## CALORIE CALCULATION METHODS

### BMR Formulas

**Mifflin-St Jeor (Recommended - Most Accurate)**
| Gender | Formula |
|--------|---------|
| Men | BMR = (10 × weight kg) + (6.25 × height cm) - (5 × age) + 5 |
| Women | BMR = (10 × weight kg) + (6.25 × height cm) - (5 × age) - 161 |

**Harris-Benedict**
| Gender | Formula |
|--------|---------|
| Men | BMR = 66.5 + (13.75 × weight kg) + (5.003 × height cm) - (6.75 × age) |
| Women | BMR = 655.1 + (9.563 × weight kg) + (1.850 × height cm) - (4.676 × age) |

**Katch-McArdle (When Body Fat % Known)**
| Formula |
|---------|
| BMR = 370 + (21.6 × Lean Body Mass in kg) |
| LBM = Weight × (1 - Body Fat %) |

### TDEE = BMR × Activity Multiplier

| Activity Level | Multiplier | Description |
|----------------|------------|-------------|
| Sedentary | 1.2 | Desk job, no exercise |
| Lightly Active | 1.375 | Light exercise 1-3 days/week |
| Moderately Active | 1.55 | Moderate exercise 3-5 days/week |
| Active | 1.725 | Hard exercise 6-7 days/week |
| Very Active | 1.9 | Very hard + physical job |

### Example Calculation

**Male, 80kg, 180cm, 30 years, Moderately Active:**
```
BMR = (10 × 80) + (6.25 × 180) - (5 × 30) + 5 = 1,780 cal
TDEE = 1,780 × 1.55 = 2,759 cal/day
```

### Calorie Adjustments for Goals

| Goal | Daily Target | Weekly Change |
|------|--------------|---------------|
| Aggressive Fat Loss | TDEE - 750 to -1000 | ~0.75-1 kg/week |
| Moderate Fat Loss | TDEE - 500 | ~0.5 kg/week |
| Slow Fat Loss | TDEE - 250 | ~0.25 kg/week |
| Maintenance | TDEE | 0 |
| Lean Bulk | TDEE + 200-300 | ~0.25 kg/week |
| Moderate Bulk | TDEE + 500 | ~0.5 kg/week |

### TDEE Components
| Component | % of TDEE | Description |
|-----------|-----------|-------------|
| BMR | 60-70% | Basic life functions |
| TEF | 8-15% | Digesting food |
| NEAT | 15-30% | Non-exercise activity |
| EAT | 5-10% | Intentional exercise |

**Sources:** Mifflin et al. (1990), ACSM guidelines, sports nutrition research
```

---

## 6.2 Macro Ratios

**Query:** "Explain optimal macro ratios for different fitness goals with: goal, protein/carbs/fat percentages, grams per kg bodyweight, meal timing recommendations. Cover: fat loss, muscle gain, maintenance, endurance."

**Response:**
```
COMPLETED - SEE DETAILED VERSION IN docs/research/NUTRITION.md

## MACRONUTRIENT RATIOS BY GOAL

### Caloric Value per Gram
| Macro | Calories/gram | TEF (% burned in digestion) |
|-------|---------------|------------------------------|
| Protein | 4 cal/g | 20-30% |
| Carbs | 4 cal/g | 5-10% |
| Fat | 9 cal/g | 0-3% |

### Protein Recommendations by Goal

| Goal | g/kg bodyweight | g/lb bodyweight |
|------|-----------------|-----------------|
| Sedentary adult | 0.8 g/kg | 0.36 g/lb |
| Fat loss (preserve muscle) | 1.6-2.4 g/kg | 0.73-1.1 g/lb |
| Muscle gain | 1.6-2.2 g/kg | 0.73-1.0 g/lb |
| Maintenance (active) | 1.2-1.6 g/kg | 0.55-0.73 g/lb |
| Endurance athletes | 1.2-1.4 g/kg | 0.55-0.64 g/lb |

### Macro Split by Goal

**FAT LOSS**
| Macro | Percentage | Per kg bodyweight |
|-------|------------|-------------------|
| Protein | 30-35% | 1.8-2.4 g/kg |
| Carbs | 30-40% | 2-3 g/kg |
| Fat | 25-35% | 0.5-1 g/kg |

**MUSCLE GAIN**
| Macro | Percentage | Per kg bodyweight |
|-------|------------|-------------------|
| Protein | 25-30% | 1.6-2.2 g/kg |
| Carbs | 45-55% | 4-6 g/kg |
| Fat | 20-30% | 0.8-1.2 g/kg |

**MAINTENANCE**
| Macro | Percentage | Per kg bodyweight |
|-------|------------|-------------------|
| Protein | 20-30% | 1.2-1.6 g/kg |
| Carbs | 40-50% | 3-5 g/kg |
| Fat | 25-35% | 0.8-1.2 g/kg |

**ENDURANCE**
| Macro | Percentage | Per kg bodyweight |
|-------|------------|-------------------|
| Protein | 15-20% | 1.2-1.4 g/kg |
| Carbs | 55-65% | 5-8 g/kg |
| Fat | 20-25% | 0.8-1 g/kg |

### Example: 80kg Male, Muscle Gain
```
Calories: 2,800 (TDEE + 300)
Protein: 160g (640 cal) - 23%
Carbs: 380g (1,520 cal) - 54%
Fat: 71g (640 cal) - 23%
```

### Priority Hierarchy
1. **Total Calories** - Most important for weight change
2. **Protein** - Critical for muscle preservation/building
3. **Carbs vs Fat Split** - Personal preference, activity dependent

**Sources:** ISSN position stands, sports nutrition research, meta-analyses
```

---

## 6.3 Meal Timing

**Query:** "Explain meal timing recommendations for fitness with: pre-workout nutrition (timing, what to eat), post-workout nutrition, meal frequency, intermittent fasting considerations."

**Response:**
```
COMPLETED - SEE DETAILED VERSION IN docs/research/NUTRITION.md

## MEAL TIMING RECOMMENDATIONS

### Pre-Workout Nutrition

| Timing | What to Eat | Example |
|--------|-------------|---------|
| 2-3 hours before | Full meal (protein + carbs + fat) | Chicken, rice, vegetables |
| 1-2 hours before | Moderate meal (protein + carbs, low fat) | Greek yogurt + banana |
| 30-60 min before | Light snack (easily digestible carbs) | Banana, toast, sports drink |
| 15-30 min before | Quick carbs if needed | Dates, gel, sports drink |

**Pre-Workout Goals:**
- Adequate glycogen stores for energy
- Amino acids in bloodstream
- No digestive discomfort
- Hydration

### Post-Workout Nutrition

| Timing | Priority | Recommendation |
|--------|----------|----------------|
| 0-2 hours | Protein | 20-40g high-quality protein |
| 0-2 hours | Carbs | 0.5-1.0 g/kg bodyweight |
| Anytime | Rehydration | 1.5L fluid per kg lost |

**Post-Workout Goals:**
- Muscle protein synthesis
- Glycogen replenishment
- Rehydration
- Recovery initiation

**The "Anabolic Window":**
- Not as narrow as once believed
- Total daily protein intake matters more
- 0-4 hours post-workout is sufficient
- More important if training fasted

### Meal Frequency

| Frequency | Research Says | Best For |
|-----------|---------------|----------|
| 2-3 meals | Equally effective for most goals | IF practitioners, busy schedules |
| 4-6 meals | Slight advantage for muscle gain | Bodybuilders, high calorie needs |
| 1 meal (OMAD) | Can work but harder to hit protein | Fat loss, specific preferences |

**Key Finding:** Total daily intake matters more than meal timing for most people.

### Protein Distribution

| Strategy | Recommendation |
|----------|----------------|
| Per meal | 20-40g protein (0.25-0.4 g/kg) |
| Pre-sleep | 40g casein or mixed protein |
| Distribution | Spread evenly across meals |
| Minimum meals | 3-4 to optimize muscle protein synthesis |

### Intermittent Fasting (IF)

| Method | Fasting Period | Eating Window |
|--------|----------------|---------------|
| 16:8 | 16 hours | 8 hours |
| 18:6 | 18 hours | 6 hours |
| 20:4 | 20 hours | 4 hours |
| 5:2 | 2 full days/week | 5 normal days |

**IF Considerations:**
- No magic fat-burning benefit (just easier deficit)
- May be harder to hit protein targets
- Works for some, not others - personal preference
- Not recommended if training fasted for muscle gain
- Fine for fat loss if total calories/protein are met

### Practical Meal Timing Schedule

**Training at 6 PM Example:**
| Time | Meal | Content |
|------|------|---------|
| 8:00 | Breakfast | Eggs, oats, fruit |
| 12:00 | Lunch | Chicken, rice, vegetables |
| 4:00 | Pre-workout snack | Banana, protein shake |
| 6:00 | Training | - |
| 7:30 | Post-workout | Protein + fast carbs |
| 9:00 | Dinner | Complete meal |
| 10:00 | Pre-sleep | Casein or cottage cheese |

**Sources:** ISSN position stands, Alan Aragon research, meta-analyses on meal timing
```
